SEMESTER S5 
MOBILE ROBOTICS  
Course Code 
PBRUT504 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCRUT402 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To give students the ability to apply mathematical modelling to kinematics, localization and 
path planning of mobile robots 
2. To give students the ability to apply various strategies to system level control of mobile 
robots 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Locomotion:  Introduction, Key issues for locomotion, Legged Mobile 
Robots - Leg configurations and stability, Wheeled Mobile Robots - 
Wheeled locomotion: the design space, Wheel design, Wheel geometry, 
Stability, Maneuverability, Controllability, Aerial robots – advantages of 
UAVs over conventional manned aircraft, Types of UAVs - Fixed-wing 
UAV or airplane – characteristics, Rotary-wing UAV - Multi-rotor, 
Tricopter, Quadcopter or quadrotor, Hexacopter, Y3/Y6, Octocopter 
Mobile Robot Kinematics:   
Introduction, Kinematic Models and Constraints - Representing robot 
position, Forward kinematic models, Wheel kinematic constraints for Fixed 
standard wheel, Steered standard wheel and Castor wheel only, Robot 
kinematic constraints 
Example of Robot kinematic models and constraints: Differential-drive robot 
only 
Mobile Robot Maneuverability - Degree of mobility, Degree of steerability, 
Robot maneuverability, Mobile Robot Workspace - Degrees of freedom, 
Holonomic robots 
 
11 

 
 
2 
Mobile Robots Fundamental problems: Path Planning, Localization, 
Sensing, Mapping, Simultaneous Localization and Mapping 
Mobile Robot Localization: Introduction, The Challenge of Localization - 
Noise and Aliasing, Localization-Based Navigation versus Programmed 
Solutions, Belief Representation - Single-hypothesis belief, Multiple-
hypothesis belief, Differences between Markov and Kalman Localization 
(detailed explanation not required) 
Representation and Reasoning about Space: Representing Space - 
Spatial 
Decomposition, 
Geometric 
Representations, 
Topological 
Representations   
Representing the Robot: Configuration Space, Simplification of C-space   
 
11 
3 
Path Planning for Mobile Robots:  
Free-space path versus Semi-free-space path, Non-homotopic paths versus 
Homotopic paths 
Constructing a discrete search space - Visibility graph, Tangent graph, 
Retraction Methods 
Searching a Discrete State Space - Graph search - Depth-first Search, 
Breadth-first Search, Dijkstra’s Algorithm, Best first search – A and A* 
Algorithm 
Searching a Continuous State Space – Potential Fields, Vector field 
histogram, Bug 1, 2 and Tangent Bug algorithms   
Probabilistic path planning – RPP, PRM, RRT 
11 
4 
System Control:   Horizontal Decomposition, Vertical Decomposition, 
Hybrid Control Architectures, Middleware, Alternative Control Formalisms, 
The Human Robot Interface 
Off-Board Communication: Tethered, Untethered – types of untethered 
communication 
 
11

SEMESTER S5 
ARTIFICIAL INTELLIGENCE FOR ROBOTICS  
 
Course Code 
PERUT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the Fundamentals of Robotics and AI: 
 
2. Utilize supervised and unsupervised learning techniques for robotic perception and action. 
3. Develop and evaluate novel AI algorithms for specific robotic applications through projects 
and case studies. 
4. Analyze recent advancements and research trends in AI and robotics. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Artificial intelligence: Introduction, its importance, The Turing test, 
Foundations of artificial intelligence, A brief historical overview, Intelligent 
Agents-Agents and Environments, Good behaviour- The concept of 
rationality, nature of Environments, structure of Agents, Expert systems -
basic overview, Application areas of AI - vision and speech processing, 
robotics. 
9 
2 
Learning - Forms of learning: Supervised Learning Algorithms- Decision 
Trees, Logistic Regression, Support vector Machines, Unsupervised 
Learning Algorithms: K-means clustering k-Nearest Neighbors, Principle 
Component Analysis, Reinforcement based learning 
9 
3 
Deep Feedforward Networks: Perceptrons – Single layer & Multi-layer, 
Learning XOR, Convolutional Neural Networks -basic outline and functions 
of each layers only, Sequence Modeling-Need for sequence models, basic 
RNN architecture and types 
9 

 
 
4 
Robotics - Robotic perception, Localization and mapping, 
Machine learning in robot Perception, Application domains. Mobile Robot 
Navigation-Path planning, Path Planning and obstacle avoidance-A* 
algorithm 
9

SEMESTER S5 
DESIGN FOR MANUFACTURING AND ASSEMBLY   
 
Course Code 
PERUT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCRUT303, 
PCRUL307
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand how design choices impact manufacturing costs and processes. 
2. To gain skills in tolerance analysis and understanding datum systems for precise 
manufacturing. 
3. To learn to minimize part count, standardize designs, and create assembly-friendly products. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Design Impact and Material Considerations - Design Impact on Cost: 
Understanding how design choices affect manufacturing costs. Design for 
‘X’ – DFM Approach: Overview of Design for Manufacturing principles and 
the DFM Framework. Material and Process Evaluation: Selecting 
appropriate materials and processes. General DFM Guidelines: Key 
guidelines for designing manufacturable products. Machining and Casting 
Guidelines and Examples: Specific considerations for machining and casting 
processes. Minimize Finishing Requirements: Strategies to reduce post-
processing needs. Facilitating Machining Design Features: Datum features, 
functional and manufacturing aspects. Component Design for Machining: 
Considerations and redesign examples. Form Design of Castings and 
Weldments: Design principles for castings and weldments. 
9 
2 
Tolerance Analysis and Selective Assembly - Tolerance Analysis: Process 
capability and metrics, cost aspects of tolerances. Feature and Geometric 
Tolerances: Understanding and applying tolerances in design. Relationship 
9 

 
 
between Tolerance Grades and Machining Processes: Attainable tolerance 
grades. Cumulative Effect of Tolerances: Sure fit law, normal law, and 
truncated normal law. Interchangeable Part Manufacture and Selective 
Assembly: Concepts and examples. Control of Axial Play: Techniques for 
controlling play, including secondary machining operations and laminated 
shims. 
3 
Datum Systems and True Position Theory - Datum Systems: Degrees of 
freedom, grouped datum systems, and their applications. Computational 
Accuracy: Translational and rotational accuracy calculations. Geometric 
Analysis: Applications of geometric analysis in design. True Position 
Theory: Understanding true position theory, including co-ordinate and 
conventional methods of feature location. Virtual Size Concept: Concepts of 
floating and fixed fasteners, projected tolerance zones. Assembly with 
Gasket and Zero True Position Tolerance: Practical applications and 
examples. Functional Gauges: Use and design of functional gauges. Paper 
Layout Gauging: Techniques and examples. 
9 
4 
Principles of Design for Assembly - Minimize Part Count: Strategies to 
reduce the number of parts in a design. Standardization and Minimize Part 
Variety: Principles of standardization and variety reduction. Design 
Guidelines for Manual Assembly: Best practices for designing for manual 
assembly. DFA Analysis: Conducting DFA analysis and calculating DFA 
index. Design for Automated Assembly: Principles and guidelines for 
automated assembly. Introduction to DFMA Software: Overview of software 
tools used for DFMA, including practical applications and case studies. 
9

SYLLABUS

No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours

ORGANISATION 
AND

FUNCTION:

of

Requirements 
of

Maintenance,

Maintenance, Overhauls and Upgrades, Breakdown Maintenance – 
Computerized Planning and Scheduling – Maintenance Repair and 
Operations – Storeroom Excellence  
9 

 
 
3

Fault-Tree Analysis – Cause and Effect Analysis – Sequence of the Events 
Analysis – The Why-Why / Root Cause Analysis, Statistical Analysis Tools 
– Failure Mode Criticality and Risk Assessment  
9 
4

Chemical, Biological, Ergonomical, Electrical - Fire: Chemistry of Fire, 
Detection and Suppression Systems – Safety Acts: Factories Act 1948, 
Environment Act 1986, OSHA, HASAWA, ISO Related to Safety

SEMESTER S5 
SIGNALS AND SYSTEMS 
 
Course Code 
PERUT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To study and analyse continuous and discrete-time signals and systems, focusing on their 
properties, representations, and necessary analytical methods.  
2. To understand signal transformation   between domains and to develop filtering methods 
based on DFT 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Elementary Signals, Classification and representation of continuous time and 
discrete time signals, Signal operations. Continuous time and discrete time 
systems – Classification. Representation of systems: Differential equation 
representation 
of 
continuous 
time 
systems. 
Difference 
equation 
representation of discrete systems. 
 
9 
2 
Sampling of continuous time signals, Sampling theorem for low pass signals, 
aliasing. Z transform, ROC, Inverse transform, properties, Unilateral 
transform. Frequency domain representation of discrete time signals, 
Discrete time Fourier series and its properties. Discrete time Fourier 
transform (DTFT) and its properties. 
 
9 
3 
The 
Discrete 
Fourier 
Transform-IDFT-Properties 
of 
DFT-Circular 
convolution – Linear Filtering methods based on the DFT- linear convolution 
using circular convolution, overlap save and overlap add methods. 
9 
4 
Computation of DFT: Radix-2 Decimation in Time and Decimation in 
Frequency FFT -Algorithms - IDFT computation using Radix-2 FFT 
9 

 
 
Algorithms. FIR and IIR Filters. - FIR Filter Structures: Direct Form, 
Cascade Form IIR Filter Structures: Direct Form, Transposed Form, Cascade 
Form and Parallel Form (Design is not required).

SEMESTER S5 
INDUSTRIAL ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PERUT526 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduce students to the fundamental concepts of industrial engineering, including its history, 
development, role, and applications. 
2. Equip students with the knowledge and skills to design, analyze, and improve production 
systems, including plant layout, line balancing, and product design. 
3. Develop students' understanding of quality control principles and techniques, including 
statistical process control, sampling inspection, and reliability engineering 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Concept of Industrial Engineering-History & development- Role of 
industrial engineer-Applications of industrial engineering. Production-
production 
function-production 
system-analysis-Productivity-factors 
affecting productivity-increasing productivity of resources. 
Plant location, Layout & Line balancing- Concept-factors governing plant 
location-location economics-Design of layout of factories-Product, process 
and combination layout-systematic layout planning. Design of assembly 
lines, Line balancing methods. Computer applications in layout designs-
CORELAP, ALDEP, CRAFT 
 
9 
2 
Product Design and Analysis – New product development – concept & 
steps- process planning and design-Value Engineering-Standardization-
Simplification- Make or Buy Decisions – Ergonomics in product design – 
Concurrent engineering 
Forecasting- Simple moving average method-weighted moving average 
 
9 

 
 
method-double moving average method- simple exponential smoothing – 
adjusted exponential smoothing- linear regression-semi average method- 
Delphi method  
3 
Inspection & Quality Control – Definition- Purpose- types- SQC-
Probability concepts- Estimation- Significance Testing- ANOVA- Sampling 
Inspection – Sampling Plans –Control charts & their applications- Life 
testing – Reliability and Reliability Prediction – Monte Carlo Simulation- 
Zero defect concept – Quality Circle 
9 
4 
Decision Making – Definition – Importance – types of Decisions – Theories 
– Techniques- Decision making process-Scientific approach- quantitative 
methods in decision making – Decision under risk – Decision under 
Uncertainty – Decision Tree 
9

SEMESTER S5 
MEASUREMENTS AND INDUSTRIAL INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
PERUT527 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarise with the measurement system and mechanism for measuring parameters 
2. To familiarise with the measurement interfaces, transmitters and Instrumentation diagrams 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to measurements systems - Methods of Measurement- 
Functional Elements of measurement system (Measurement System 
Architecture)- Examples of measurement systems-Standards Used in 
Measurements- Electrical Standards- Time and Frequency - Physical 
Standards -Basic SI Units-Calibration- process of calibration-methods- 
Expression of uncertainty- Accuracy and Precision -indications of precision, 
significant figures-  
Errors in Measurements - Static error, static correction, Propagation of 
errors, Systematic and Random errors in measurement -  
Statistical Evaluation of measured data: Histogram, Mean, Measure of 
dispersion from the mean, Range, Deviation, Average deviation, Standard 
Deviation, Variance  
Design of measurement systems-Example 
 
9 
2 
Force measurement -Introduction to force measurement-Spring Balance -
Load cells – Elastic load cells and Strain gauge load cell -Piezoelectric force 
transducers. 
Torque measurement – Introduction to torque measurement-Strain gauge 
torque meter- Inductive torque meter-optical torque measurement.  
 
9 

 
 
Displacement Measurement (Linear and Angular): Optical Encoders -
Synchro/Resolver Sensors -Time of Flight Ultrasonic Sensors- Laser 
Interferometers 
Speed measurement – Introduction to Speed measurement -Mechanical 
tachometer (Revolution counter)– electrical tachometer (Eddy current 
tachometer)-optical tachometer (Stroboscopic tachometer) 
Acceleration-Strain gauge-based accelerometers Quartz accelerometers 
MEMS accelerometers 
Thickness Measurement- Micrometers- Laser scanners  
Position, Location and Altitude Measurement-MEMS devices -Global 
Positioning System (GPS)  
Range measurement – Laser range sensor  
Slant angle measurement – tilt sensor  
3 
Optical Variables Measurement - Photometry 
and Radiometry-
Photomultipliers -photodiodes Charge coupled devices (CCD cameras) 
Radiation Measurement -Basic principle - Geiger Muller counter – 
Scintillation counter 
Thermal Variables Measurement-Temperature measurement- Thermistors-
Thermopile-Infrared sensors - Pyroelectric sensors- Sensor ICs - LM34, 
LM35, Thermal Imaging -Calorimetry 
Pressure measurement -Bourdon tubes-Fiber optic pressure sensor-  
Differential pressure transmitter for pressure measurement-Dead weight 
tester 
Vacuum measurement-Thermal Conductivity gauge, Pirani Gauge 
Flow Measurement - Electromagnetic Flow meters -Ultrasonic Flow 
meters- Thermal Mass Flow meters- Flow transmitter 
Humidity measurements-Definitions and units-psychrometer, dew point 
hygrometer, electrical resistive hygrometer 
Qualitative and Quantitative methods of chemical measurement - Beer- 
Lambert’s law Spectrometry – NMR – Chromatography  
9  
4 
Smart transmitters: Transmitters-types of signals- pneumatic instrument 
communication signals (3-15 psig, )- electronic instrument communication 
signals (4-20 ma), signal transducers_ I to P converter, P to I converter- 
features of smart and intelligent transmitters- smart transmitter with HART 
communicator. 
Digital interfaces in measurement systems: IEEE -488_ instrumentation 
bus (GPIB)- objectives of industrial communications - serial data 
 
9 

 
 
communications links- RS-232C and D interfaces- RS-422, RS-423 and RS-
485 interfaces - Communication protocols- field bus-profibus-modbus-
foundation fieldbus. 
Instrumentation diagrams: instruments' labeling- ISA standards-Data 
Sheets- P&ID diagrams.

SEMESTER S5 
ALGORITHMS AND DATA STRUCTURES 
 
Course Code 
PERUT 528 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
GBEST204 
       Programming in C Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the principles of algorithm analysis, including time and space complexity. 
2. Analyse the complexity of algorithms using asymptotic notations. 
3. Implement linear and non-linear data structures. 
4. Illustrate various techniques for searching and sorting. 
5. Design algorithms using fundamental design techniques: greedy, divide and conquer, and 
dynamic programming. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Algorithms 
Performance Analysis- Space Complexity, Time Complexity, Asymptotic 
Notation-Big Oh, Big Omega, Big Theta, 
Complexity Calculation of Simple Algorithms 
Introduction to Data Structures 
Definition, Classification of Data Structures: Primitive and Non-primitive, 
Linear and Non-linear, Operations on Data structures 
 
9 
2 
Linear data structures  
Array: Representation of arrays, Applications of arrays 
Stack: Definitions & Concepts, Operations on Stacks, Applications of 
Stacks-Infix to postfix conversion, Postfix Evaluation 
Queue: Definitions & Concepts, Operations on Queue, Types of queue -
Circular Queue, Priority Queue, Applications of Queue 
9 

 
 
Linked lists: - singly linked list, doubly linked list, Circular linked list, 
operations on linked, Application of linked list-memory management-first 
fit, best-fit, worst-fit  
3 
Non-linear data structures 
Tree-Terminologies, Representation, Types, Traversals 
Graph-Terminologies, Representation, Traversal-DFS, BFS, Minimum 
spanning tree-Kruskal’s, Prim's algorithm, Shortest path-Dijkstra’s algorithm 
9 
4 
Searching and Sorting Algorithms 
 Linear search, Binary search, Bubble sort, Selection sort, Insertion sort, 
Quick sort, Merge sort. 
Hashing-Hash table, Hashing functions 
Algorithm Design: Greedy algorithm, Divide and conquer, Dynamic 
programming, Backtracking, Branch and bound, 
 
9

Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
ROS Fundamentals:

9 
2

a More Sophisticated Action Server, Using the More Sophisticated Action. 
9

in

and 
formats,

playing back data, Techniques for building maps from sensor data, 
GMapping and Cartographer for mapping, Map Server in ROS, Loading and 
serving maps, localization techniques (e.g., AMCL), Implementing 
localization in ROS.

SEMESTER S5 
AUTOMATION LABORATORY 
Course Code 
PCRUL507 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks  
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None  
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart practical knowledge on various industrial automation technologies. 
2. To understand the functioning and programming of Programmable Logic Controllers (PLCs). 
3. To develop skills in electro-pneumatic and electro-hydraulic systems. 
4. To simulate and control industrial processes using SCADA. 
5. To familiarize with Automation Studio software for designing and simulating automation 
systems 
 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments 
1 
 Introduction to PLC 
o 
Understanding PLC hardware and software. 
o 
Basic programming in Ladder Logic. 
2 
 PLC Programming - I 
o 
Development of basic automation tasks using PLC. 
o 
Simple start-stop circuits. 
 
3 
 PLC Programming - II 
o 
Advanced PLC programming concepts. 
o 
Timer and counter functions. 
 
4 
 Basic Pneumatic Systems 
o 
Introduction to pneumatic components.

 
 
o 
Designing and implementing basic pneumatic circuits. 
 
5 
 Electro-Pneumatic Systems 
o 
Integration of electrical control with pneumatic systems. 
o 
Troubleshooting electro-pneumatic circuits. 
 
6 
 Basic Hydraulic Systems 
o 
Introduction to hydraulic components and systems. 
o 
Designing basic hydraulic circuits. 
 
7 
 Electro-Hydraulic Systems 
o 
Integrating electrical control with hydraulic systems. 
o 
Practical implementation and troubleshooting. 
 
8 
 Introduction to SCADA Systems 
o 
Basics of SCADA. 
o 
Configuring SCADA for monitoring and control applications. 
 
9 
 SCADA Simulation 
o 
Simulating industrial processes using SCADA. 
o 
Developing human-machine interfaces (HMIs). 
 
10 
 Automation Studio Software 
o 
Designing and simulating automation systems using Automation Studio. 
o 
Final project integrating PLC, pneumatic, hydraulic, and SCADA 
systems. 
 
11 
 Comprehensive Project 1 
 
Experiment: Combine PLC and SCADA systems into a single automated 
process. 
 
12 
 Comprehensive Project 2 
 
Experiment: Combine PLC, electro-pneumatic, and electro-hydraulic 
systems into a single automated process.

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding 
of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
 

 
 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or 
quality of program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER 6 
ROBOTICS AND AUTOMATION 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
SEMESTER S6 
ROBOTIC CONTROL SYSTEMS 
 
Course Code 
PCRUT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Model the systems using transfer function approach as well as state space approach 
2. Employ time domain analysis to predict and diagnose transient performance parameters of the 
system for standard input functions. 
3. Compute the time domain and frequency domain specifications of a system 
4. Analyse dynamic systems for their stability and performance using root locus and  Bode plot 
5. Analyse systems using state space approach 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Control System- Definition, Open loop vs closed loop control systems- 
components of a typical control system- Necessity of a control system in a 
Robot, Linear time invariant Systems- Transfer function, Necessity of 
knowing the transfer function, 
Modelling –Mechanical Translational and Electromechanical systems (Force 
voltage and Force current analogy) . block diagram representation -Block 
diagram reduction, signal flow graph, Basic problems using Masons gain 
formula. 
 
11  
2 
Time domain analysis of control systems: Transient and steady state 
responses - time domain specifications - first and second order systems - step 
responses of first and second order systems. Steady state error analysis - 
static error coefficient of type 0,1, 2 systems .Concept of stability: Time 
response for various pole locations - stability of feedback system -Routh's 
 
11  

 
 
stability criterion. 
3 
Root locus - General rules for constructing Root loci –stability from root 
loci - effect of addition of poles and zeros. 
Frequency domain analysis: Frequency domain specifications (derivations 
not required)- Analysis based on Bode plot -Log magnitude vs. phase plot. 
Design of P, PI and PID controller using Ziegler-Nichols tuning method. 
11  
4 
State space analysis of systems: Introduction to state concept - state equation 
of linear continuous time systems, matrix representation of state equations. 
Phase variable and canonical forms of state representation-controllable, 
observable, -state transition matrix, relationship between state equations and 
transfer function. Controllability &observability-Kalman’s method. State 
feed-back design via pole placement technique. 
 
11

Course Objectives:

2. To give students the ability to apply robotics to various services 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Field Robots - Definition 
Robotics in Agriculture and Forestry: Forestry -   Technological 
Developments, Robot Locomotion in Forestry, Forestry Automation, 
Machine Perception and SLAM in the Forest Environment, Autonomy, 
Teleoperation, and Fleet Management, Autonomous Robots for Silviculture 
and Treatment, Broad Acre Applications in Agriculture -  Overview of 
Automatic Guidance, Sowing, Weeding, Spraying, and Broad-Acre 
Harvesting, Horticulture -  Picking of Fruit and Vegetables, Color Sorting 
and Produce Grading, Livestock Management -  Robot Milking, Sheep 
Shearing, Livestock Inspection, Robotic Animals, Unmanned Vehicles in 
Agriculture, Applications of robots in Precision agriculture, Greenhouse 
farming, Seeding and harvesting, Aerial robots and Ground Robots for 
Agriculture 
 
Environmental 
Monitoring 
and 
Disaster 
Management 
Robots:   
Environmental Monitoring - Environmental Sensing, Sensors, Sensor 
Networks, Early Environmental Robotics, Energy-Efficient Sampling 
Platforms, Natural Habitat Mapping, Marine and Atmospheric Plume 
 
9  

 
 
Detection and Localization, Data Muling WSNs, Robotics in Disaster 
Management -  Surveying and Mapping, Rescue, Reconstruction 
Case Studies: Any one general application each of robotics in  Agriculture 
and Forestry,  Environmental Monitoring and Disaster Management 
2 
Construction and Infrastructure Robots:  Automation and robotics in 
the construction sector and precast concrete industry,  timber construction,   
steel component production,  Service robot systems and humanoid 
construction robots,  Guidelines for construction robot development,  
Strategies for an automation and robot oriented construction process,  
Construction components for a robot oriented design & construction -  
Clear product structure,  Design focused on simplicity, handling and 
assembly,  Families of components,  Component interfaces,  Integral 
product structures,  The accuracy problem, Robots in Inspection and 
Monitoring of Buildings and Infrastructure:  Unmanned Aerial Vehicle 
(UAV), Unmanned Ground Vehicles (UGV), Wall-Climbing Robots, 
Cable-Crawling Robots, Marine Robots, Hinged Microbots, Legged 
Robots, Hybrid Robots, Multi-Robot Systems 
Mining Robots:  Scope for Robotics in Mining - Underground Transport, 
Drilling, Explosive Placement, Secondary Rock Breaking, Metalliferous 
Roadway Development, Geology-Based Guidance Systems 
Military and Defence Robots:  Applications of robots in military and 
defence 
 Case Studies: Any one general application each of robotics in   
Construction  and Infrastructure, Mining, Military and Defence  
 
9  
3 
Marine and Underwater Robots: Types of Underwater Vehicles – 
Submarines, Submersibles, ADS, ROVs, AUVs, Hybrid Underwater 
Vehicles, Basics of moving a vehicle through water – Newton’s Laws, 
Forces on Underwater Vehicles, Navigation – Specifying Position or 
Location – Landmarks, Dead Reckoning, Standard Coordinate Systems and 
GPS, Triangulation, Navigational Instruments  
Case Study: A detailed look at a Work Class ROV – mechanical 
subsystems, Power source, Control room, Operations, crew, Deck cables, 
umbilical and tether, LARS, the ROV  
Space Robots:   Orbital Robotic Systems, Surface Robotic Systems, 
Planetary Rovers – Architecture, Mission Planning, Propulsion and 
Locomotion, Planetary Navigation 
Educational and Entertainment Robots: Role of robots in Education, 
9  

 
 
Case Study:  Any one general application each of robotics in   Education 
and Entertainment 
4 
Service Robots: Definition, Mapping and Navigation for Service 
Robots: Map Building and Localization - Localization with Wi-Fi and 
Other Networked Radio Communications, Ultra Wideband Localization, 
Radio Frequency Identification Localization, North-Star Active Infrared 
Localization - Two-dimensional planar code localization, Laser-ranging 
localization, 
Camera-Based 
Localization, 
Time-of-Flight 
Camera 
Localization, Navigation, Path Planning, and Obstacle Avoidance - 
Structured Light Obstacle Avoidance, Linear and Planar Distance Sensors 
and Obstacle Avoidance, Optic Flow, Ground-Plane Segmentation, and 
Feature-Based Obstacle Avoidance, Optimization of Path Planning for 
Obstacle Avoidance, Optimization of Robot Behavior and Interaction for 
Obstacle Avoidance 
 
Household Service Robots: Introduction, Work Environments for 
Household Service Robots, Functionalities of Household Service Robots 
Examples of Service Robotic System Design:  
Surveillance Robot – Introduction, Block diagram of the system, System 
Initialization - Passive Acoustic Location, Target Detection Using the 
Frame Differencing Method, Feature Selection and Segmentation, Video 
Surveillance - Tracking Using Particle Filter, Target Model Update, 
Abnormal Behavior Detection, MFCC Feature Extraction, Support Vector 
Machine 
Service Robot for Elders - Robot System - System Architecture, Hardware 
Structure, Human Robot Interaction - Touch and Watch Interaction, Speech 
Interaction, Motion Interaction 
Medical and Healthcare Robots: Key Benefits, Surgical Robots - Surgeon 
extender robots, Auxiliary surgical support robots, Control Paradigms in 
Surgical Robots, Other Applications of Robots in Healthcare 
Logistics Robots: Application areas of robots in Logistics, Warehouse 
robots – Types of Warehouse Robots

SEMESTER S6 
 ADVANCED INDUSTRIAL AUTOMATION  
 
Course Code 
PERUT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide an in-depth understanding of advanced industrial automation systems and 
technologies. 
2. To develop the ability to design, implement, and manage automation solutions for industrial 
applications. 
3. To develop proficiency in programming and using Programmable Logic Controllers (PLCs). 
4. To foster an understanding of the integration of automation with business and manufacturing 
processes 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Advanced Industrial Automation- Automation Hierarchy: 
Field, Control, and Supervisory Levels. Sensors and Actuators: Types of 
Sensors, Signal Conditioning, Types of Actuators. Communication Protocols 
in Automation 
Safety in Automation Systems, Data Acquisition and Monitoring. Human-
Machine Interface (HMI).  Communication Protocols in Automation, 
Modbus, Profibus, Ethernet/IP. 
 
9  
2 
Advanced Control Systems- Control System Fundamentals 
Open-loop vs Closed-Loop Control, PID Control 
PID Tuning Methods. Distributed Control Systems (DCS), 
Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA) 
Advanced Control Strategies: Feedforward Control, 
 
9  

 
 
Cascade Control, Model Predictive Control (MPC). 
Case Studies and Applications. 
3 
Advanced PLC Programming and Applications: Advanced PLC 
Programming Techniques, Timers, Counters, and Sequencers. PLC 
Networking and Communication, SCADA Systems. Data Acquisition and 
Monitoring, PID Control using PLCs. PLC Troubleshooting and 
Maintenance, Industrial Applications of PLCs, Case Studies and Real-world 
Examples. 
9  
4 
Recent Trends in Industrial Automation - Industrial Internet of Things 
(IIoT), Big Data Analytics in Automation, Cybersecurity in Industrial 
Automation, Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning in Automation, 
Digital Twin Technology, Integration of Control Systems with IT Systems, 
Case Studies on Smart Factories and Industry 4.0. Future Trends and 
Innovations in Industrial Automation. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
MECHATRONIC SYSTEM DESIGN 
 
Course Code 
PERUT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Focus on understanding the interdisciplinary nature of mechatronics and the synergy between 
various components to create efficient and reliable systems. 
2. Enable students to develop and apply advanced modeling, simulation, and control techniques 
for mechatronic systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Overview of Mechatronics 
Definition, scope, and applications of mechatronic systems. 
Interdisciplinary approach: integration of mechanical, electronic, and 
software components. 
 
9  
2 
Mechanical Components 
Introduction to mechanical components: actuators, sensors, and mechanical 
structures. 
Selection criteria and compatibility considerations. 
Electronic Components 
Overview of electronic components: microcontrollers, sensors, and signal 
conditioning circuits. 
Interfacing techniques and circuit design for integration. 
 
9   
3 
Modeling Techniques 
Introduction to modeling methodologies: mathematical, physical, and 
empirical models. 
Modeling mechanical, electrical, and control subsystems. 
9  

 
 
Simulation Tools 
Hands-on experience with simulation software (e.g., MATLAB/Simulink, 
LabVIEW). 
Simulating mechatronic systems to analyze performance and behavior. 
4 
Control Theory Basics 
Introduction to control systems: feedback, PID control, and system stability. 
Design considerations for mechatronic control systems. 
Implementation and Testing 
Practical implementation of control algorithms on hardware platforms. 
Testing and validation of mechatronic systems using simulation and real-
world experiments. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
ELECTROMAGNETICS 
 
Course Code 
PERUT634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
1.Mathematics course 
including calculus, vector 
calculus, and differential 
equations. 
2.GBPHT121Physics for 
Engineers 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarize the students with the fundamentals of electrostatics, magnetostatics, time-
varying fields and electromagnetic waves. 
 
2. To equip students with expertise in analysing transmission line parameters, and utilizing 
the Smith chart for effective impedance matching and VSWR calculations. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Co-ordinate Systems: Rectangular, Cylindrical and 
Spherical Co- ordinate Systems – Co-ordinate transformation,  
Vector Calculus: Gradient of a Scalar field, Divergence of a Vector field 
and Curl of a Vector field- their physical interpretation; Divergence 
Theorem, Stokes’ Theorem 
 
9  
2 
Electrostatics: Coulomb’s Law, Electric field intensity, Electric Flux and 
Flux Density; Gauss’s law and its application to determine the field due to 
an 
infinite 
line 
charge, 
infinite 
sheet 
charge; 
Poisson’s 
and 
Laplace’equations 
Magnetostatics: Biot-Savart’s Law, Magnetic Field intensity, Magnetic 
flux, Magnetic flux density, Magnetic Scalar and Vector Potential, Ampere’s 
circuital law and simple applications; Continuity equation for current, 
 
9  

 
 
Maxwell’s equation from fundamental laws. 
3 
Wave Propagation: Wave Equations from Maxwell's Equations; Solution of 
Wave equation Uniform Plane Waves, Propagation of Uniform Plane waves 
in free space, lossless and lossy dielectric medium, good conductor- phase 
velocity and group velocity, Intrinsic Impedance, Attenuation constant and 
Propagation constant in all medium; Skin effect and skin depth, Poynting 
Vector and Poynting Theorem, Wave polarisation and types of polarisation. 
9  
4 
Transmission Lines: Uniform lossless transmission line - line parameters, 
Transmission line equations & solutions, Propagation constant, 
Characteristic impedance, Wavelength, phase velocity and group velocity, 
Derivation of input impedance of transmission line, Reflection coefficient 
and VSWR, Transmission line as circuit elements (L and C), Development 
of Smith chart, Calculation of line impedance and VSWR using smith chart. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
QUALITY AND RELIABILITY 
Course Code 
PERUT636 
 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Demonstrate the approaches and techniques to assess and improve process and/or product 
quality and reliability.  
2. Introduce the principles and techniques of Statistical Quality Control and their practical uses 
in product and/or process design and monitoring 
3. Illustrate the basic concepts and techniques of modern reliability engineering tools. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Quality value and engineering – quality systems Quality engineering in 
product design and production process – system design, parameter design, 
tolerance design, Quality costs – quality improvement 
 
9  
2 
Statistical Process control - X, R, p, c charts, other types of control charts, 
process capability, process capability analysis,  
process capability index.  
Acceptance sampling by variables and attributes, design of sampling plans, 
single, double, sequential and continuous sampling plans, design of various 
sampling plan 
 
9  
3 
Loss function, tolerance design – N type, L type, S type; determination of 
tolerance for these types. Online quality control– variable characteristics 
attribute characteristics, parameter design.  
9  
4 
Quality function deployment – House of quality, QFD matrix, and total 
quality management concepts. Quality information systems, quality circles, 
introduction to ISO 9000 standards.  
Reliability– Evaluation of design by tests - Hazard Models, Linear, Raleigh, 
9  

 
 
Wei bull. Failure Data Analysis, reliability prediction based on wei bull 
distribution, Reliability improvement.

ENERGY SYSTEMS 
  
 
Course Code 
PERUT637 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3

2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduces various types of renewable energy sources 
2. Various means of generating and storing energy and the importance of renewable energy 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Energy Scenario: Indian Energy Scenario, World Energy Scenario, Indian 
Energy Sector Reforms, Energy and Environment, Energy Security, Energy 
conservation act  
Energy Efficient Systems: Reducing pollution and improving efficiency in 
buildings, Green Building Standards, Types of lamps and their efficiencies 
9  
2 
Renewable Energy Resources: Solar Thermal System-Working Principle-
Block diagram, Solar Photovoltaic System- Working Principle-Block 
diagram, Solar cell efficiency calculation, Wind Energy Systems- Working 
Principle-Block diagram, wind power equation, Energy from Waves and 
tides- Working Principle-Block diagram, Ocean Thermal Energy System- 
Working Principle-Block diagram, Energy from Biomass 
9 
3 
Energy Storage: Importance of Energy Storage- Means of Storing Energy- 
Principle of operation and performance comparison. Compressed air storage, 
Fly wheel Energy Storage, Battery Storage-Battery: Specification, 
Charging/Discharging rate, Primary and secondary cells-Dry cell, lead acid, 
lithium ion, Lithium air, Nickel Cadmium, Nickel Metal Hydride Fuel Cell: 
Working Principle, efficiency 
9 

 
 
4 
Energy Standards – International Energy Standards-ISO50001, Bureau of 
Energy Efficiency, star rating  
Energy Management: Significance and general principles of Energy 
Management, Energy audit-types and procedure, Energy audit report, 
Instruments for energy auditing 
Energy Economics: Traditional Types of Rates - Single-Part Rates - Two-
Part Rates - ThreePart Rates – Numerical problems 
9

SEMESTER S6 
COMPILER DESIGN AND OPERATING SYSTEMS  
 
Course Code 
PERUT638 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PERUT 528 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand theory of compiler implementation, compiler parsing 
techniques, intermediate machine representation and optimization. 
 
2. To impart fundamental understanding of the purpose, functions and the key design issues 
of an operating system. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to compilers-Phases of compiler, The role of Lexical Analyzer, 
Role of the Parser, Basic parsing approaches - Eliminating left recursion, left 
factoring. Top-Down Parsing - Recursive Descent parsing, Nonrecursive 
Predictive Parsing, Bottom-up parsing-Shift Reduce Parsing, Simple LR 
Parser, More Powerful LR Parsers 
9  
2 
Syntax directed definitions-Inherited and Synthesized Attributes. S- 
attributed definitions, L- attributed definitions. Intermediate Code 
Generation-Variants of Syntax Tree. Three address code-Quadruple, Triple. 
Run Time Environments, Local optimizations, Principal Sources of 
Optimizations. 
9  
3 
Operating system overview - Functions, Service - System calls, Types-
System boot process. 
Processes: Process states, Process control block, threads, scheduling, -Inter-
process communication - shared memory systems, Message passing systems. 
Process Scheduling: Basic concepts- Scheduling criteria -Scheduling 
algorithms- First come First Served, Round robin scheduling 
9  

 
 
4 
Process synchronization: Race conditions – Critical section problem – 
Peterson’s solution - Semaphores – Synchronization problems - Producer 
Consumer. 
Deadlocks: Necessary conditions, Resource allocation graphs - Deadlock 
avoidance – Banker’s algorithms. 
Memory Management: Concept of address spaces, Contiguous memory 
allocation, fixed and variable partitions. 
File System: File concept - Attributes, Operations, types 
9

SEMESTER S6 
INDUSTRIAL INTERNET OF THINGS 
 
Course Code 
PERUT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs.30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
UCEST105  
Algorithmic Thinking 
with Python
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To understand the basic concepts of Industrial Internet of Things (IIoT) systems. 
2. 
To become proficient in the design, development and implementation of IIoT systems  
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to IoT and IIoT: IOT Definition, Importance of IoT, IoT 
architecture, Technology Behind IoT - Server End Technology, Sources of 
Internet of Things, M2M Communication. IoT Application Areas. 
The Various Industrial Revolutions, Role of Internet of Things (IoT) & 
Industrial Internet of Things (IIoT) in Industry, Industry 4.0 revolutions, 
Support System for Industry 4.0. 
9 
2 
Implementation Systems for IIoT: Sensors and actuators for industrial 
processes, sensor networks: network topologies, types of networks. Study of 
different sensors and their characteristics: Light sensor, temperature sensor 
with thermistor, voltage sensor, ADC and DAC, Temperature and Humidity 
Sensor DHT11, Motion Detection Sensors, Wireless Bluetooth Sensors, 
Level Sensors. Actuators: Thermal, hydraulic, pneumatic, electromechanical. 
Communication Protocols: UART Communication Protocol, I2C Protocol 
device interfacing and decoding of signal, SPI Protocol device interfacing 
and decoding of signal. Application layer protocols: HTTP, CoAP, MQTT. 
9 

 
 
3 
Data Handling in IIoT: Role of microcontrollers in IIoT: Introduction to 
Raspberry Pi-Installation, programming, Interfaces (serial, SPI, I2C) 
Cloud Services:  Configuration of the cloud platform, Sending data from the 
IoT nodes to the gateways using different communication options; 
Transferring data from gateway to the cloud. Google, AWS, Microsoft Azure 
cloud architect. 
Case study: Program different Sensors for IoT applications 
Security and privacy issues in IoT 
9 
4 
Industrial IoT Applications:  Healthcare, Power Plants, Inventory 
Management & Quality Control, Plant Safety and Security (Including AR 
and VR safety applications), Facility Management. Oil, chemical and 
pharmaceutical industry, applications of UAVs in industries 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10

SEMESTER S6 
SOFT COMPUTING AND COMPUTER VISION FOR ROBOTS  
 
Course Code 
PBRUT604 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Equip students with a solid understanding of the basic principles and significance of soft 
computing techniques, including fuzzy logic, genetic algorithms, and neural networks, and 
their differentiation from traditional hard computing methods 
 
2. Introduce students to the concepts of hybrid systems such as neuro-fuzzy and genetic fuzzy 
systems, and provide a foundational understanding of machine learning techniques, including 
supervised, unsupervised, and reinforcement learning 
3. Enable students to grasp the fundamental concepts of computer vision 
4. Enable students to apply different vision algorithms for industrial applications. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Fundamentals of Soft Computing : 
Definition and significance of soft computing; Differences between hard and 
soft computing, Introduction to Fuzzy Logic: Fuzzy Sets and Membership 
Functions, Fuzzy Rules and Inference Systems. Introduction to genetic 
algorithms-Working Principle, Operators: Selection, crossover, and 
mutation. Introduction to neural networks, Learning rules and various 
activation functions, Single layer Perceptrons multilayer perceptrons, 
Backpropagation algorithm, Architecture 
 
11 
2 
Hybrid systems for Computer vision- Neuro-fuzzy systems, Genetic fuzzy 
system (Concept only). Introduction to Machine Learning in Robotics-
Supervised and unsupervised-learning, Reinforcement learning (Concept 
 
11 

 
 
only). Basics of Soft Computing Tools and Platforms: Open-source libraries 
(TensorFlow, Keras) (simple programs only) 
3 
Introduction to Computer Vision: Industrial Machine Vision  
Basic concepts of image formation: Radiometry and geometric 
transformations. 
Geometric 
Camera 
Models-Pinhole 
camera 
model,Perspective projection and camera parameters. Techniques for 3D 
reconstruction. Spatial domain and Frequency domain methods for image 
enhancement. 
Image 
Segmentation: 
Thresholding., 
Region-based 
segmentation. 
11 
4 
Pattern Analysis 
Clustering: K-Means, Mixture of Gaussians, Classification: Discriminant 
Function, Supervised, Un-supervised, Semi-supervised; Classifiers: Bayes, 
KNN, ANN models;  
Dimensionality Reduction: PCA, LDA, ICA 
Vision algorithms: Vision algorithms for identifying end wires- binary vision 
algorithm, grey-scale vision algorithm, active ranging using structured light 
technique in industrial vision 
 
11

SEMESTER S6 
DESIGN THINKING AND PRODUCT DEVELOPMENT 
(Common to Group A & Group B) 
Course Code 
GXEST605 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
2:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To guide students through the iterative stages of design thinking, including empathizing with 
users, defining problems, ideating solutions and developing Proof of Concepts (PoC) and 
technical feasibility studies. 
2. To promote the development of critical thinking skills by engaging students in integrative 
inquiry, where they ask meaningful questions that connect classroom knowledge with real-
world applications. 
3. To equip students with the ability to involve in product design considering the sustainability, 
inclusivity, diversity and equity aspects. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of design thinking and product development: Overview of 
stages of product development lifecycle; Design thinking -Definition-Design 
thinking for product innovation; Bringing social impact in ideation-
Identifying societal needs-understanding multi-faceted issues-community 
engagement and empathetic design- technological innovation meeting 
societal needs; Understanding and Bridging the divide using Human 
Centered Design (HCD); Designing for inclusivity in product development-
embracing user diversity - Long term impact - sustainability encompassing 
environmental,economic and social dimensions; Technology Readiness 
Level in the Innovation Life-cycle; Performing a self-check on innovative 
6 

 
 
ideas - Originality of idea- understanding innovation landscape - 
patentability - understanding the economic landscape - Unique Selling 
Proposition (USP) - Repeatability and Manufacturability - Sustainability - 
Leveraging business models for comprehensive analysis 
2 
Empathize: Design thinking phases; Role of empathy in design thinking; 
Methods of empathize phase - Ask 5 Why/ 5 W+H questions;  Empathy 
maps -  Things to be done prior to empathy mapping - Activities during and 
after the session; Understanding empathy tools - Customer Journey Map - 
Personas. 
Define: Methods of Define Phase: Storytelling, Critical items diagrams, 
Define success. 
6 
3 
Ideation : Stages of ideation; Techniques and tools - Divergent thinking 
tools - Convergent thinking tools - Idea capturing tools; Cross-industry 
inspiration; Role of research in ideation - Market research - consumer 
research - leveraging research for informed ideation; Technological trends - 
navigating the technological landscape - Integrating emerging technologies; 
Feasibility studies - technical, economic, market, operational, legal,  and 
ethical feasibility; Ideation session- techniques and tips. 
Proof of Concept (PoC) : Setting objectives; Risk assessment; Technology 
scouting; Document and process management; Change management; 
Knowledge Capture; Validating PoC; Story telling in PoC presentation 
6 
4 
Design: Navigating from PoC to detailed design; Developing Specification 
Requirement Document (SRD)/Software Requirement Specification (SRS); 
Design for manufacturability; Industrial standards and readability of code; 
Design to cost; Pre-compliance; Optimized code; Design Failure Mode and 
Effects Analysis (DFMEA); Forecasting future design changes. 
Prototyping: Alpha prototypes; Beta prototypes; Transition from design to 
prototype; Goals and expectations for Alpha and Beta prototypes; Effective 
strategies for maintaining timeline in prototyping; Testing and refining 
Alpha prototypes; Transitioning to Beta prototypes. 
Pilot build: Definition and purpose of a pilot build; setting objectives; 
Identification and selection of manufacturing partner for pilot build; Testing 
procedures in pilot build; Scaling from pilot build to full-scale production / 
implementation. 
6

Sample Assignments: 
1. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including inclusivity, diversity and equity are taken 
into consideration during the empathize and define phases of the Miniproject course. 
2. Evaluate and prepare a report on how the aspects including sustainability, inclusivity, diversity and 
equity are taken into consideration during the ideate phase of the Miniproject course. 
3. Evaluate and prepare a report on how User-Centric Design (UCD) is used in the design and 
development of PoC of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
4. Prepare a plan for the prototype building of the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
5. Report on the activities during the empathize phase including the maps & other materials created 
during the sessions. 
6. Report on the activities during the define phase including the maps & other materials created during 
the sessions. 
7. Report of all the ideas created during the ideation phase of the Miniproject course through the tools 
including SCAMPER technique, SWOT analysis, Decision matrix analysis, six thinking hats 
exercise 
8. Prepare a full scale production plan for the product being developed in the Miniproject course. 
9. Create a Stanford Business Model Canvas related to the Miniproject. 
An industrial visit of at least a day for experiential learning and submit a report on the learnings, for 
example industry standards and procedures.

SEMESTER S6 
FUNDAMENTALS OF ROBOTICS 
 
Course Code 
OERUT611 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand and discuss the Robotic systems on the basis of various parameters 
2. Provide insight into the types of sensors and actuators used in robotics 
3. Explain the various types of end effectors. 
4. Educate on the principles of kinematics and motion planning. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definitions- Robots, Robotics; Types of Robots- Manipulators, Mobile 
Robots-wheeled & Legged Robots, Aerial Robots; Anatomy of a robotic 
manipulator-links, joints, actuators, sensors, controller; open kinematic vs 
closed kinematic chain; degrees of freedom; Robot considerations for an 
application- number of axes, work volume, capacity & speed, stroke &reach, 
Repeatability, Precision and Accuracy, Operating environment, point to 
point control or continuous path control. Robot Applications- medical, 
mining, space, defense, security, domestic, entertainment, Industrial 
Applications-Material handling, welding, Spray painting, Machining. 
 
9  
2 
Sensors and Actuators 
Sensor classification- touch, force, proximity, vision sensors. Internal 
sensors-Position sensors, velocity sensors, acceleration sensors, Force 
sensors; External sensors-contact type, noncontact type; Vision - Elements of 
vision sensor, image acquisition, image processing; Selection of sensors. 
 
9  

 
 
Actuators for robots- classification-Electric, Hydraulic, Pneumatic actuators; 
their advantages and disadvantages; Electric actuators- Stepper motors, DC 
motors, DC servo motors and their drivers, AC motors, Linear actuators, 
selection of motors; Hydraulic actuators- Components and typical circuit, 
advantages and disadvantages; Pneumatic Actuators- Components and 
typical circuit, advantages and disadvantages. 
3 
Robotic configurations and end effectors 
Robot configurations-PPP, RPP, RRP, RRR; features of SCARA, PUMA 
Robots; Classification of robots based on motion control methods and drive 
technologies; 3R concurrent wrist; Classification of End effectors - 
mechanical grippers, special tools, Magnetic grippers, Vacuum grippers, 
adhesive grippers, Active and passive grippers, selection and design 
considerations of grippers in robot. 
9  
4 
Kinematics and Motion Planning 
Robot Coordinate Systems- Fundamental and composite rotations, 
homogeneous co-ordinates and transformations, Kinematic parameters, D-H 
representation, Direct Kinematics. The Arm equation forward Kinematic 
analysis of a typical robots up to 3 DOF. Motion Planning- joint space 
trajectory planning-cubic polynomial, linear trajectory with parabolic blends; 
Cartesian space planning, Point to point vs continuous path planning. 
 
9

SEMESTER S6 
INTRODUCTION TO INDUSTRIAL AUTOMATION  
 
Course Code 
OERUT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarise students with industrial automation 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Automation methodologies: Concept of Mechanization and Automation, 
Types of Automation, Automated flow lines, Fundamentals of Transfer 
Lines. Trends in manufacturing – GT and Cellular Manufacturing, Flexible 
manufacturing systems – features of FMS, Computer integrated 
manufacturing – Need for AI and expert systems in CIM, Automated 
assembly system – flexible assembly automation,  
 
9  
2 
Elements of CNC systems: servomotor and servo system design trends, 
stepper motors and controls, Automated tool changers and pallet changers. 
Material Handling and Identification Technologies: Overview of Material 
Handling Systems, Principles and Design Consideration, Material Transport 
Systems, Storage Systems, Automated Storage and Retrieval Systems, 
Overview of Automatic part Identification Methods, Automatic Guided 
Vehicles. Sensor systems for automated inspection, Automatic gauging and 
size control systems, thickness measurement, Machine vision systems. 
 
9  
3 
Sensors and actuators for automation, Classification of position, proximity 
and motion sensors, electromechanical switches, LVDT, RVDT. Electrical, 
Hydraulic, and pneumatic actuators and their comparison (Concept only), 
Examples - use of Electrical, Hydraulic, and Pneumatic actuators in 
industrial automation.  
9 h 

 
 
Pneumatic/Hydraulic Automation: control valves – direction, pressure and 
flow, sequential control of single /multiple actuator systems, cascade and 
Karnaugh Veitch map methods.  
Electro pneumatic/electrohydraulic automation: Symbols: Basic electrical 
elements – relay, solenoid, timers, pneumatic – electrical converters, 
Design of circuits and hands on models on material handling systems. 
 
4 
Automation Control: Sequence control and programmable controllers – 
logic control and sequencing elements, Programmable Logic Controller – 
Architecture, PLC ladder diagram, Relay logic, Analog and digital I/Os, 
Timers, Counters, Program control instructions. Case studies on PLC 
ladder programming.  
SCADA – Building blocks of SCADA systems, RTU and HMI subsystem, 
Architecture of Distributed Control System (DCS), Interfacing PLC to 
SCADA/DCS using communication link (RS232, RS485), Protocols 
(Modbus ASCII/RTU) and OPC. 
  
 
9

Course Objectives: 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to CAD and CAM: Overview of CAD/CAM, Importance in 
modern manufacturing, Manufacturing Planning and Control, Overview of 
Manufacturing Planning, Key aspects of Manufacturing Control 
Introduction to CIM: Concepts and significance of CIM, CIM system 
components: hardware and software, Production Types and Models, Types 
of production: batch, mass, and continuous, Manufacturing models and 
metrics, Automation and Lean Production, Basic elements of an automated 
system, Levels of automation, Lean Production and Just-In-Time (JIT) 
principles 
9  
2 
Production Planning, Control, and CAPP: Process Planning and CAPP, 
Steps in Computer-Aided Process Planning, Benefits and implementation of 
CAPP, Production Planning Techniques, Aggregate Production Planning, 
Master Production Schedule 
Material Requirement Planning (MRP) and Capacity Planning: 
Introduction to MRP, Techniques for Capacity Planning 
Control Systems and Shop Floor Control: Overview of manufacturing 
control systems, Shop floor control techniques 
Inventory Control and ERP: Basic principles of inventory control, 
Introduction to Manufacturing Resource Planning-II (MRP-II): Overview of 
Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP) 
9  

 
 
3 
Cellular Manufacturing and Group Technology: Group Technology (GT) 
and Part Families, Concept of Group Technology 
Classification and coding of part families: Production Flow Analysis, 
Techniques for production flow analysis, Benefits of production flow 
analysis 
Cellular Manufacturing Concepts: Composite part concept, Designing and 
layout of machine cells 
Quantitative Analysis in Cellular Manufacturing: Rank Order Clustering 
Method, Arranging machines in a GT cell using Hollier Method 
Machine Cell Design and Layout: Principles of machine cell design, 
Layout strategies for cellular manufacturing 
9  
4 
Advanced Manufacturing Systems: Flexible Manufacturing Systems 
(FMS), Types and components of FMS, Applications and benefits, Planning 
and control of FMS 
Automated Guided Vehicle Systems (AGVS): Overview of AGVS, 
Applications and benefits, Vehicle guidance technology 
Vehicle Management and Safety in AGVS: Techniques for vehicle 
management, Safety considerations in AGVS 
Industrial Robotics: Anatomy and classification of robots, Robot control 
systems and end effectors, Sensors in robotics 
Robot Accuracy and Applications: Robot accuracy and repeatability, 
Industrial applications of robots 
9

Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the Fundamentals of Robotics and AI: 
 
2. Utilize supervised and unsupervised learning techniques for robotic perception and 
action. 
3. Develop and evaluate novel AI algorithms for specific robotic applications through 
projects and case studies. 
4. Analyze recent advancements and research trends in AI and robotics.

Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description

basic overview, Application areas of AI - vision and speech processing, 
robotics.

SEMESTER: S6 
ROBOTICS AND MACHINE VISION LAB 
Course Code 
PCRUL607 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:2:0 
ESE Marks   
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCRUT402  
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Develop Kinematic Models and Verify Performance 
2. 
Familiarise Trajectory Planning Techniques 
3. 
Implement Advanced Control Strategies 
4. 
Integrate Sensing and Localization Techniques 
5. 
Implement deep learning algorithms for object detection and tracking 
 
 
 
 
 
Expt.  
No. 
Experiments 
1 
Programming of Robotic Manipulators 
2 
Obtain forward and inverse kinematic models (check end effector and joint positions with 
theoretical and actual values) 
3 
Trajectory Planning for Robotic Manipulators(Joint space and Cartesian space trajectory 
planning 
4 
Control of Mobile Robots-  
Control of mobile robot for moving to a point(xg, yg) , following a line 
(ax+by+c=0),moving to a specific target orientation (θg) (Closed loop control considering 
kinematic models)
5 
Obstacle avoidance for a Differential Drive Robot using Ultrasonic Sensor 
6 
Localization of a Mobile Robot using LIDAR 
7 
Calibration of Sensors 
8 
Deep Learning based Object Detection and Tracking using Yolo Algorithm 
9 
Visual Servoing- to enable the robotic arm to autonomously locate and manipulate objects 
based on visual feedback from an attached camera.
10 
Target Tracking from a Moving Vehicle

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding 
of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 
Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 

 
 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or 
quality of program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 
Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Basic knowledge about networking in industries. 
2. Understand the evolution of computer networks using the layered network architecture. 
3. Understand the concepts of data communications 
4. Be familiar with the Transmission media and Tools 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Modern instrumentation and control systems – OSI model – Protocols – 
Standards – Common problems and solutions – Grounding/shielding and 
noise - EIA-232 interface standard – EIA-485 interface standard – Current 
loop and EIA-485 converters. FIBRE OPTICS: Introduction – Fibre optic  
cable components and parameters – Basic cable types – Connection fibres – 
troubleshooting 
9 
2 
MODBUS  
Overview – Protocol structure – Function codes – Modbus plus protocol –
Data Highway – AS interface (AS-i) –Device Net: Physical layer – 
Topology – Device taps – Profibus PA/DP/FMS: Protocol stack – System 
operation 
9 
3 
ETHERNET SYSTEMS  
IEEE/ISO standards – Medium access control – frames – Reducing collisions 
– Auto negotiation – LAN system components – Structured cabling – 
Industrial Ethernet – Troubleshooting Ethernet. CAN BUS: Concepts of bus 
access and arbitration – CAN: Protocol-Errors: Properties – detection –
processing – Introduction to CAN 2.0B 
9 
4 
WIRELESS COMMUNICATIONS  
Radio spectrum – Frequency allocation – Radio modem – Intermodulation – 
Implementing a radio link – RFID: Basic principles of radio frequency 
identification – Transponders – Interrogators. 
 APPLICATIONS 
Automotive communication technologies – Design of automotive X-by-Wire 
systems (Assignment only) 
9

1 
Introduction: Characteristics of non-linear systems -  Methods of analysis – 
Classifications of nonlinearities – Common physical nonlinearities – 
Saturation or limiter – Deadzone or Threshold – Types of relays - Types of 
springs – Backlash in Gears – Inherent nonlinearity. 
Linearisation of Nonlinear system - Autonomous and non autonomous 
systems-modelling of simple pendulum- mass spring system. 
9 
2 
 Phase plane analysis 
Phase Plane Analysis: Singular points- Phase portraits – Analytical method 
for the construction of Phase trajectories –  
Graphical method f construction of Phase trajectory – Isoclines Method –  
Analysis and classification of singular points -  
Local behaviour of nonlinear systems -  Limit cycles on phase plane - 
Stability- poincare- bendixon theorems. 
9 
3 
Describing function analysis 
Describing Function: Definition - Describing Function Analysis- Describing 
functions of Typical nonlinearities- Ideal Relay – Relay with deadzone – 
Simple deadzone – Saturation or Limiter  
9 

 
 
Closed loop stability using describing function- Stability of limit cycles – 
Accuracy of describing function analysis - Relative stability from describing 
from describing function. 
4 
Stability of the system- Lyapunov Stability Theory  
Stability of nonlinear systems- Concept - equilibrium points- stability in 
small and stability in large- Lyapunov’s stability definitions –  Localisation 
and stability in the small - Stability by the method of Lyapunov – First 
methd of Lyapunov- Concept of Lyapunov’s stability theorems -  Sign 
definiteness of scalar function  Lyapunov stability theorems  - Stability of 
nonlinear system by method of Lyapunov – Krasovskii’ theorem- Variable 
gradient method of generating Lyapunov function 
9

SEMESTER S7 
DESIGNING THE MECHANISMS FOR AUTOMATED MACHINES 
Course Code 
PERUT743 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course is designed to build a basic understanding on the various concepts involved in the 
design of different mechanisms of automated machines.  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Automated Systems 
Overview of Automated Systems: Structure of automatic industrial systems, 
Linear and circular configurations, Non-industrial robots 
Manufacturing Process Layouts: Processing layout, Case studies: Chain 
links, springs, soldering printed circuits, galvanizing steel strips, Approaches 
to automating manufacturing processes, Timing layout and productivity 
determination, 
9  
2 
Drive Systems and Dynamic Analysis  
Mechanical and Electromagnetic Drives: Mechanical drive systems: Falling 
weight, inclined belt, spring systems, Electromagnetic drives and electric 
drives: Induction motors, stepper motors 
Hydraulic and Pneumatic Drives: Hydraulic and pneumatic drives, Brakes 
and variable moment of inertia 
Dynamic Analysis: Calculation of selection parameters, Calculation of 
braking time for different systems 
9 
3 
Kinematics and Control  
Kinematics and Control Mechanisms: Position function and input-output 
relations, 4 slot Geneva mechanism, cam mechanisms, Amplifiers and 
flexible cam systems 
9  

 
 
Dynamic Accuracy and Damping: Dynamic accuracy and vibrations, 
Damping: Electrical and mechanical 
4 
Transportation, Feeding, and Functional Systems  
Transportation Devices: Linear and rotational transportation Conveyors, 
indexing tables, Case studies on transportation devices 
Feeding and Orientation Devices: Feeding systems: Liquid, powder, wire, 
rod 
Orientation: Passive, active, logical, and electromagnetic fields 
Functional Systems and Manipulators: Automatic assembling and inspection 
systems, Manipulators: Dynamics, kinematics, vibrations 
9

SEMESTER S7 
ANALOG AND DIGITAL COMMUNICATION 
Course Code 
PERUT744 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the concept of analog communication. 
2. To analyse different digital communication schemes. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Analog Communication 
Block diagram of a communication system. Need for analog modulation. 
Amplitude modulation. Equation and spectrum of AM signal. DSB-SC and 
SSB systems. Block diagram of SSB transmitter and receiver. Frequency and 
phase modulation. Narrow and wide band FM and their spectra. FM 
transmitter and receiver. 
 
9  
2 
Stochastic processes and Source coding 
Review of probability. Bayes theorem and conditional probability. 
Stochastic processes, Stationarity. Conditions for WSS and SSS. 
Autocorrelation and power spectral density. LTI systems with WSS as 
input. Sampling and Quantization. Pulse code modulation, Transmitter and 
receiver. Companding. Practical 15 level A and mu-law companders. 
DPCM transmitter and receiver. Delta modulation. 
 
9  
3 
G-S Procedure and Effects in the Channel 
Definition of signal .Basic operation on signals. Gram-Schmitt procedure. 
Signal space. Baseband transmission through AWGN channel. Inter 
Symbol Interference. Nyquist criterion for zero ISI. Raised cosine and 
Square-root raised cosine spectrum, Partial response signalling and 
 9  

 
 
duobinary coding. Equalization. Vector model of AWGN channel. Matched 
filter and correlation receivers. MAP receiver, Maximum likelihood 
receiver and probability of error.  
4 
Digital Modulation Schemes 
Digital modulation schemes. Baseband BPSK system and the signal 
constellation. BPSK transmitter and receiver. Base band QPSK system and 
Signal constellations. Plots of BER Vs SNR with analysis. QPSK transmitter 
and receiver. Quadrature amplitude modulation and signal constellation. 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
OPERATIONS RESEARCH   
Course Code 
PERUT746 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basics of operations 
research- 
OR 
models- 
applications, 
Linear 
programming: problem formulation-Graphical method-simplex method- Big 
M method-Two phase method-Duality in linear programming. 
 
9  
2 
Transportation 
Problem: 
Formulation- 
balanced 
& 
unbalanced 
transportation problems, method for finding initial solution- North west 
corner method- Least cost entry method-Vogel’s approximation method 
(VAM), test for finding optimality- MODI method. 
Assignment Problem: Formulation-optimal solution- Hungarian Algorithm-
Variants of assignment problems. 
 
9 
3 
Introduction to queuing theory: terminologies- classification of queuing 
models- Kendall’s notation-Single server models Multi server models. 
Network analysis: basic terms- network construction-time analysis-Critical 
Path Method (CPM)-Programme Evaluation Review Technique (PERT). 
9  
4 
Decision theory: steps in decision theory approach-decision making 
conditions- decisions under risk-decision under uncertainty conditions- 
decision tree analysis. 
Game theory: games with saddle points- Dominance property- games 
without saddle points for 2x2 games- graphical method for m x 2 & 2 x n 
games. 
 
9

SEMESTER S7 
POWER ELECTRONICS 
 
Course Code 
PERUT747 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the basic principles of power electronics and the characteristics of power 
semiconductor devices. 
2. To design various power converter circuits including rectifiers, DC-DC converters, inverters, 
and AC-AC converters. 
3. To learn the application of power electronics in controlling electric drives and power systems. 
4. To explore the emerging trends and technologies in power electronics and their applications 
in automation and robotics. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Power Semiconductor Devices: Power Diodes, TRIACs, 
GTOs, Power BJTs, Power MOSFETs, and IGBTs. Thyristors, Static and 
Dynamic Characteristics. Gate characteristics. Firing methods. Gate drive 
circuits. Thyristor protection circuits. Series and parallel combinations. 
Commutation types (no analysis). 
9 
2 
AC-DC Converters: Single-phase Uncontrolled and Controlled Rectifiers. 
Three-phase Controlled Rectifiers. Inductive, and Capacitive Loads. Power 
Factor Improvement in Rectifiers. DC-DC Converters: Step up and step 
down Chopper. Buck, Boost, Buck-Boost Converters. Isolated and non-
isolated converters 
9 
3 
Inverters: Single-phase and three-phase inverters. Voltage source inverters – 
series, parallel, and bridge inverters – current source inverters. 1800 and 
1200 modes. PWM inverters. 
9 

 
 
AC-AC Converters: Single-phase and three-phase AC-AC Converters. 
Cycloconverters (single phase) 
4 
Applications of Power Electronics: D.C Motor control -  phase control, 
Single phase SCR drive, Three phase SCR drive, Chopper controlled DC 
drives. A.C. Motor control: Controlled – slip system and slip power recovery 
system, stepper motor drive. UPS, Battery charging techniques. Recent 
Developments in Power Electronics for Automation and Robotics. 
9
